  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText5723120675654615190" style="display:none">Princess Winter is admired for her grace, kindness and beauty, despite the scars on her face. She's said to be even more breath-taking than her stepmother, Queen Levana...<br /><br />When Winter develops feelings for the handsome palace guard, Jacin, she fears the evil Queen will crush their romance before it has a chance to begin.<br /><br />But there are stirrings against the Queen across the land. Together with the cyborg mechanic, Cinder, and her allies, Winter might even find the power to launch a revolution and win a war that's been raging for far too long.<br /><br />Can Cinder, Scarlet, Cress, and Winter claim their happily ever afters by defeating Levana once and for all?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5723120675654615190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<a href="/questions/407007-so-if-winter-is-based-off-of-snow-white">So if winter is based off of snow white wouldnt cinder, kai, cress, thorn, wolf, scarlat, and iko the 7 dwarfs???</a>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/47847343-amanda"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/47847343-amanda">Amanda</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">NO! Cinder is Cinderella, Kai is the Cinderella Prince, Cress is Rapunzel, Thorne is Eugene (Tangled) or the prince that saves Rapunzel from the tower<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">NO! Cinder is Cinderella, Kai is the Cinderella Prince, Cress is Rapunzel, Thorne is Eugene (Tangled) or the prince that saves Rapunzel from the tower, Scarlet is Red Riding Hood, Wolf is the wolf in Red Riding Hood and Iko does not belong to any of these fairy tail but she is... the most cool and beautiful android in New Beijing! The only characters from Snow White are Jacin (Prince Charming), Winter (Snow White)and Levana (The Evil Queen, the fairest of them all)<br />Oh, and NO!, EVEN IF WINTER IS BASED OFF FROM SNOW WHITE IT DOESNT MEAN THE OTHER CHARACTERS ARE THE 7 DWARFS, DONT YOU DARE DEMEAN AND DEGRADE THEM LIKE THAT! Sorry, I love the Lunar Chronicles and I just want other people to respect them as I do. I am a full time fangirl, if you are one too, you will understand the pain of disrespectfulness to our fandoms. Dont feel offended!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<a href="/questions/164258-how-come-if-the-book-winter-is-less-pages">How come if the book Winter is less pages than the book Cress, how come it is going to take so long until its publication? Is research needed or is there some kind of delay, maybe it&#39;s going to be published around that time for the next christmas because of the ironic name of the book? I&#39;m not sure but it would be interesting to know.</a>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6268473-kameron-b-moore"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1524080698i/6268473._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6268473-kameron-b-moore">Kameron B. Moore</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The page number listed there is not accurate: it's an approximation based on her previous books. On her blog, Marissa Meyer has stated that WINTER is <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The page number listed there is not accurate: it's an approximation based on her previous books. On her blog, Marissa Meyer has stated that WINTER is the biggest book out of them all, and she won't reveal how big until closer to the publication date. Also, page number has nothing to do with how slow or fast something is published: it is based on the author and the publisher's release schedule. Hope this helped!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1098450862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098450862" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1098450862?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1098450862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17451002262394631266"><blockquote>
  <i>“She was prettier than a bouquet of roses and crazier than a headless chicken. Fitting in was not an option.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>And... I've finished! *sob*<br/><br/>The last few weeks have been a whirlwind of Lunar Chronicles. After finally giving in and picking up <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206760.Scarlet__The_Lunar_Chronicles___2_' title='Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scarlet</a>, even though I hated <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_' title='Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinder</a>, I just haven't been able to get enough of this series. And this longass final installment was a <b>heart-pounding, fast-paced finale</b>.<br/><br/>You know, I actually checked and this is the <b>longest YA book I have ever read</b> at over 820 pa</span>
  <span id="freeText17451002262394631266" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“She was prettier than a bouquet of roses and crazier than a headless chicken. Fitting in was not an option.”</i>
</blockquote><br />And... I've finished! *sob*<br /><br />The last few weeks have been a whirlwind of Lunar Chronicles. After finally giving in and picking up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206760.Scarlet__The_Lunar_Chronicles___2_" title="Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a>, even though I hated <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a>, I just haven't been able to get enough of this series. And this longass final installment was a <b>heart-pounding, fast-paced finale</b>.<br /><br />You know, I actually checked and this is the <b>longest YA book I have ever read</b> at over 820 pages, the second longest being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/444327.Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix__Harry_Potter___5_" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (Harry Potter, #5) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a> at 766 pages. I was a bit concerned seeing as I generally think any YA book over 500 pages feels too long, but I needn't have worried. I flew through this monster.<br /><br />I've come to the conclusion that I <i>really</i> like how Meyer balances retelling with the traditional story. She gets the amount of each just right, changing up enough to keep it surprising and exciting, but slotting in many parallels to the original stories that often catch me by surprise and make me smile.<br /><br />I also love how far the relationships have come. Lots of funny and touching dynamics, <b>lots of great friendships to remind us that romance isn't everything</b>. <br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a>, I loved the title character so much. In addition to the brave, level-headed Cinder, the fiery Scarlet, and the sweet, intelligent Cress, we now have Ms beautiful and crazy. Each character is very different, but important in her own way, and together they make a funny, lovable team.<br /><br />The book wraps up very well, delivering a <b>dramatic and bloody climax</b>. There are many close calls, lots of action, and lots of crazy. As I've said about the previous two books: this might not be great literature, but it sure is a rush of wild excitement.<br /><br />And can we all just take a moment to talk about how great Thorne is? I compared him to Gilderoy Lockhart in my review of the last book and he is still my favourite character. He's just so hilarious and ridiculous... in the best way.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Thorne scoffed. “Careful is my middle name. Right after Suave and Daring.”<br />“Do you even know what you're saying half the time?” asked Cinder.<br />***<br />“A kiss from the Captain would probably melt my central processor.”<br />Thorne winked at her. “Oh trust me. It would.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>I am such a fangirl</b>. Now I just need to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25689074.Stars_Above__The_Lunar_Chronicles_" title="Stars Above (The Lunar Chronicles) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Stars Above</a> during the long wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18584855.Heartless" title="Heartless by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Heartless</a>.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17451002262394631266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13673377684603988149" style="display:none">*** <b>MARISSA MEYER IS FINISHED WITH WINTER!!</b> ***<br><br><br><b>TEASERS (from Marissa Meyer's Twitter):</b><br><br>She screamed like a thousand birds were picking at her flesh. <br>She screamed like the palace was burning down around her.<br><br>“Hold these wires and make sure they don’t touch.”<br>“What happens if they touch?”<br>“The ship will probably self-destruct.”<br><br>She was going to have to train herself not to stare at him quite as often as she was used to. That would be no easy task.<br><br>“May I request a new uniform? A towel seems inappropriate for the position.”<br><br>She was a danger to his hard-earned neutrality. Thinking about her tended to give him an unwanted hitch in his lungs.<br><br>“We have had word that some political groups are calling for the forced abdication of Emperor Kaito."<br><br>"Being raised on Luna seems to really mess people up. She wouldn’t be the lovable cyborg we’ve all come to adore."<br><br>“They’re the first crew I’ve ever had, and most of them even call me Captain. I’m going to miss them.”<br><br>When they arrived, they arrived in force—a dozen military ships surrounding the safe house, guns drawn.<br><br>Her whole body was wound up tight. She was ready to storm the palace herself—an army of one.<br><br>It did not feel like home. It felt like a place that had been built to be paradise, but had become a prison.<br><br>“Greenwich is a funny word, isn’t it? All green and witchy. Like soup.”<br><br>Fear was a weakness in the court. Much better to act unperturbed. Much safer to act crazy, when in doubt.<br><br>In a moment of weakness, he craned his head and kissed her on the shoulder, where the drop of blood had fallen before.<br><br>He laughed, like someone had stabbed him in the chest and he had no other choice but to find it amusing.<br><br>She was prettier than a bouquet of roses and crazier than a headless chicken. Fitting in was not an option.<br><br>“Oh, stars. I don’t know his real name. How can I not know his real name? What kind of alpha mate am I?”<br><br>"She definitely has a crush on you. It’s about the size of Jupiter.”<br><br>She had the bone structure of a bird. Wolf probably could have crushed her with his fingertips.<br><br>"You’re a good guy, Thorne.” She paused. “Well, you have your moments." <br><br>"People do not put their faith in phantoms.”<br><br>“I expected palm trees and red carpets,” said Iko, brow drawn in a show of severe disappointment.<br><br>“Right now, a kiss is the going rate for near-death experiences. It’s kind of a point system.”<br><br>She still looked furious, but now she also looked a little intimidated. Not intimidated enough, but a little.<br><br>“I don’t hear anything.”<br>“Exactly. That’s what happens when you *stop talking*.”<br><br>Over a dozen thaumaturges were stationed around the room. It was almost like the queen expected someone to start trouble.<br><br>Being tyrannized by Levana had a way of making allies of enemies.<br><br>"I intend to put an end to the rumors of the darling Princess Selene once and for all.”<br><br>Levana already wanted her dead. She couldn’t very well want her *more* dead.<br><br>If she’d learned anything from Thorne, it was that sometimes gumption was all a person really needed to be heroic.<br><br>“You are a child playing at war games,” he said, “and you’re too naive to realize that you’ve already lost.”<br><br>“All I ever wanted were two legs, ten fingers, and perfect hair. Is that really so much to ask?”<br><br>“But I forgot my ball gown on Earth.” “Don’t worry. You wouldn’t want to get blood all over it anyway.”<br><br>Instead of being pieced together with wires and steel, these creatures were a jigsaw of muscle tissue and cartilage.<br><br>***<br><br><b>"Winter is the evil queen's stepdaughter. She's lived on Luna in the palace but grown up with her stepmother and seen how, when Levon uses her lunar powers, it's turned her into such a tyrant. Winter has decided never to use her lunar gift. But when a lunar chooses not to use their gift, it slowly starts to drive them crazy, so Winter is afflicted with bad hallucinations, and as the book goes on, her mental state is slowly deteriorating."</b><br><br>***<br><br><b>"Book Four: WINTER is based on Snow White, where we will finally get to see the world of the Lunars."<br><br>THE WORLD OF LUNARS!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/628120.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>***<br><br>... the moon?<br><br>o_o</span>

<div id="review_2253667587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2253667587" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2253667587?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall">2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253667587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer549835222375446636"><b>Fantastic end to a great series</b><br/><br/>This series actually got <b>better with every book. </b> <br/><br/>If you are on the fence after reading Cinder, <b>I urge you to keep going.</b> <br/><br/>Each book follows a different couple but we still have the previous couples running around throughout the story arc.<br/><br/> This time we follow <b>Winter (Snow White) and Jacin (the Huntsman).</b> Despite having no royal blood, Winter is the Lunar Princess. <br/><br/>Like most Lunars, Winter has <b>the gift of manipulation.</b> Unlike most Lunars, she would <b>rather lose her mi</b></span>
  <span id="freeText549835222375446636" style="display:none"><b>Fantastic end to a great series</b><br><br>This series actually got <b>better with every book. </b> <br><br>If you are on the fence after reading Cinder, <b>I urge you to keep going.</b> <br><br>Each book follows a different couple but we still have the previous couples running around throughout the story arc.<br><br> This time we follow <b>Winter (Snow White) and Jacin (the Huntsman).</b> Despite having no royal blood, Winter is the Lunar Princess. <br><br>Like most Lunars, Winter has <b>the gift of manipulation.</b> Unlike most Lunars, she would <b>rather lose her mind</b> than manipulate her citizens. <br><br>Winter's stepmother, the Lunar Queen (Levanna), set her sites on Emperor Kai (the Emperor of Commonwealth (essentially China)). <br><br>Once she has Kai, and his country, in her clutches then she can finally start her bid for world dominance AND <b>get rid of Princess Winter (permanently).</b> <br><br>But first, Queen Levanna must marry the young emperor.<br><blockquote>
<i>(<b>Aside: </b>Why Kai? He is <b>literally half her age</b> and his only contribution is of a <b>damsel in distress.</b> What was the point of all those tutors if all he manages to do is almost get married and kidnapped?)</i> <blockquote><i>(<b>Aside to the Aside: </b>I really liked how all the guys (for once) were the ones being rescued in a fairytale)</i></blockquote>
</blockquote><b>Cinder and her merry gang of modern fairytale friends</b> must find a way to stop this wedding and save their planet. <br><br>Told from alternating perspectives, we follow each couple - Cinder (Cinderella) and Kai (the Prince); Scarlet (Little Red Riding Hood) and Wolf (the Big Bad Wolf); Cress (Rapunzel) and Thorne (the Prince) - almost equally throughout the book. <br><br>As before, <b>Cress and Thorne are my absolute favorite couple</b> - I just adore her bravery in the face of crippling shyness. <br><br>And Thorne's charisma and adoration towards Cress just cinch this couple. Every moment where they got closer to the big kiss had me clutching the book and crossing my fingers. <br><br><b>Wolf was by far my favorite character </b>and finally we get his perspective - there's something so neat about getting the "monster" point of view. <br><br>There was <b>one thing that really frustrated me</b> about this whole series: <blockquote>
<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517275652ra/24963405.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote> Seriously. If you are <b>going to kill someone - <u><i>MAKE SURE THEY'RE ACTUALLY DEAD!</i></u></b> <br><br>Half the plot was someone finding out that an assassination didn't work and the supposed-to-be-dead character was wreaking havoc elsewhere.<br><br>Overall - this was a fun end to a thrilling series. I'm really looking forward to the companion novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25689074.Stars_Above__The_Lunar_Chronicles___0_5__0_6__1_5__3_1__4_5_" title="Stars Above (The Lunar Chronicles, #0.5, 0.6, 1.5, 3.1, 4.5) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Stars Above</a>!<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>--Rather well-read by Rebecca Soler. She certainly had a way with words. Winter's sing-songy voice was fabulous and Scarlet's french accent was rather good. Though, if both Cinder and Kai came from the Commonwealth, futuristic China, then I thought there should be an Asian accent, no?<br><br>If you are curious about Rebecca Soler, check Tucker the Reader's <a href="https://tuckerthereader.wordpress.com/2019/04/30/interview-with-rebecca-soler/" rel="nofollow noopener"> interview</a>!<br><br><i>The Finer Books Club - 2018 Reading Challenge: A retelling of a classic</i><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="549835222375446636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1153134052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1153134052" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1153134052?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1153134052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9576660893060906448"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Even in the Future the Story Begins with Once Upon a Time.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Once Upon a Time</b>, there was a lonely girl who dreamed too much. Her name was Katerina. She used to gaze at the sky and observe the faint light of the moon. One night, she watched a falling star and made a wish. She wished that she would belong. <b>Escape. Travel. Feel.</b> Little did she know that her heart's desire was about to be granted. For when the star landed on Earth, it took a woman's form. In some stories they call her the</span>
  <span id="freeText9576660893060906448" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Even in the Future the Story Begins with Once Upon a Time.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Once Upon a Time</b>, there was a lonely girl who dreamed too much. Her name was Katerina. She used to gaze at the sky and observe the faint light of the moon. One night, she watched a falling star and made a wish. She wished that she would belong. <b>Escape. Travel. Feel.</b> Little did she know that her heart's desire was about to be granted. For when the star landed on Earth, it took a woman's form. In some stories they call her the fairy god-mother. In this one, they call her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4684322.Marissa_Meyer" title="Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Marissa Meyer</a>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429025867ra/14517502.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She's our princess. And she's coming home.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Marissa Meyer searched for the best way to make wishes come true, but the answer was simple. Her words, her words would be a gift to mankind. She chose to narrate the <b>classic tales</b> everyone loved from a different angle, adding <b>space</b> and <b>androids</b> and <b>plagues</b> and <b>monsters</b>. Adding <b>diverse heroes and heroines</b>, characters of different color and weight and height and backround. Adding <b>strong friendships, sweet romances, vivid adventuress, loathsome villains and a handful of stardust</b>. And she created The Lunar Chronicles. She created <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471464575ra/20057813.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Invade Luna. Start a rebellion. End a war.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Katerina found in Winter everything she ever wanted. She read about Snow White, who was beautiful and kind, crazy and delusional, who hallucinated and sang eerie songs, who was in love with her best friend and guard. She read about Cinder, who tried to be brave and make difficult desicions that would result in sacrifices and bloodbath in order to take her throne back. About Scarlet, fierce and bold and determined Scarlet, who felt that she didn't fit in until she found her home in the face of a predator, a killer. About Cress, who dreamed about happily ever afters and pretended she was a hero from a movie when she was afraid, and didn't realize how valuable she was. These four girls were different, but were bound together by a common goal and a friendship that didn't know planets and social status.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Help me. Fight for me. And I will be the first ruler in the history of Luna who will also fight for you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>She also read about Kai, who was smart and selfless and put the welfare of his people above his own happiness. About Wolf, who was savage and murderous but also a soft cupcake who fought for his humanity. About Thorne, who was funny and cocky and didn't believe he was a hero until a strange girl turned his world upside down with her faith in him. About Jacin, who was intimidating and cold, eager to do anything for his princess. <br><b>Four boys, four girls and one android.</b> Katerina loved them all, for their strangeness and their flaws, their loyalty and their hearts. Her own heart broke when they were seperated, when they were forced to do terrible things or went through terrible things. She <b>shed tears</b> of joy and tears of sadness.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471466443ra/20057979.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>She <b>laughed</b> until her stomach hurt.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Thorne scoffed. “Careful is my middle name. Right after Suave and Daring.”<br>“Do you even know what you're saying half the time?” asked Cinder.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>She followed them through <b>riots and executions, battles and toe-curling kisses, powerful declarations and hilarious banters</b>. She did find Winter a little long, but stars above! a part of her didn't want it to end. She hated goodbyes.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“They're the first crew I've ever had and most of them even call me Captain. I'm going to miss them.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Once Upon a Time,</b> Katerina finished Winter. She held the book against her heart and looked at the sky. There it was. A Rampion, whose passengers were <b>a mechanic and an emperor, a farmer and a soldier, a hacker and a smuggler, a princess and a guard</b>. They looked down and smiled at her. She smiled back. <br>She was not alone.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471466443ra/20057980.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✨ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183237483?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder review</a><br>✨ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183237129?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet review</a><br>✨ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183237156?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Cress review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9576660893060906448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_736677230" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/736677230" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14461220-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458426069p2/14461220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/736677230?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/14461220-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer736677230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer362904522660073707"><u>AFTER READING</u><br/>I write this review 3 months after finishing the book to give me the space to think about why I was so disappointed by this book so much. This review is definitely not representative of the majority opinion, and one I never expected to hold before reading this book. Don't get me wrong though. I was SO EXCITED for this book as it was the conclusion to what is a wonderful series. Maybe I was expecting too much, or perhaps I have changed as a person since reading the first three books,</span>
  <span id="freeText362904522660073707" style="display:none"><u>AFTER READING</u><br>I write this review 3 months after finishing the book to give me the space to think about why I was so disappointed by this book so much. This review is definitely not representative of the majority opinion, and one I never expected to hold before reading this book. Don't get me wrong though. I was SO EXCITED for this book as it was the conclusion to what is a wonderful series. Maybe I was expecting too much, or perhaps I have changed as a person since reading the first three books, but this book fell flat on so many levels.<br><br>1. At a stunning 824 pages, <i>Winter</i> is a book lover's dream book size, especially when the book is [insert positive adjective here]. When I found out how long the book was, I was so ready to enjoy and savor each page. Rather, I found myself lost, annoyed, and dissatisfied. <br><br>The problem lied in that there was too much going on. Despite the immense page length + because of the cumulative nature of the series, it felt like the 8 main characters were fighting for page time to the point that no character had much/any development. <br><br>The strength of this series lies in the characters vs. the plot. The strength in a fairy tale comes not from the predictability of the plot where good will always triumph, but from the characters you meet along the way. The plot, instead of giving the characters the space to grow, became the centerpiece of <i>Winter</i>. (don't get me wrong though. some books can pull off being centered on plot, but <i>Winter</i> is not one of them)<br><br>2. This book was supposed to be about Princess Winter based off the title. But was it really though? Because I clearly did not see it. I loved the character of Princess Winter, but felt like no attention was given at all to her. Even worse, it felt like she was simply a means to advance the plot. So much potential ... and it was wasted. ^ this is a point building off my first point where the character of Winter felt like an additional tack to be tacked on to a series burgeoning with such rich characters.<br><br>3. disclaimer: I am a sucker for romance, but literally ALL the main characters were paired up by the end. 4 couples. It is to the point where the romance felt too constructed and forced (to be honest).<br><br>4. Wolf. Love the character, but because of the aforementioned problem of too many things going on, his character's journey felt so ... anticlimactic. There was this huge buildup throughout the entire novel over Wolf ... and then his journey and change ends up not serving any actual purpose or character development. Wolf, the character, fell victim to the plight of plot for plot's sake (the worst).<br><br>5. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This book was essentially a cycle of characters being captured and held hostage by Levana <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> LOL.<br><br>6. Death in books usually need to serve a purpose for me, but there was just so much senseless death in this book that honestly did not make any sense. Rather than feeling remorse, sadness, regret, etc. I instead felt confusion and had the reaction of, "huh" "like why". <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There is a literal massacre of the Lunar people where the violence and death reach a point of ludicrosity. And even worse, it is not even talked about or a major concern to Cinder or the other main characters ... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>7. Cinder, the main character of this entire series, did not feel like the Cinder I grew to love over the course of this series!! <br><br>8. This book is SO lookist. This was my biggest contention with the author. &gt;:/ *commence rant* <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The end of the book makes it seem like Levana should be dethroned NOT because she has committed genocide, or tried and successfully killed thousands, if not millions of people through biowarfare, or even the other countless crimes that she has committed. NOPE. Levana should be dethroned because she is ... (wait for it) ugly. !!! LITERALLY WHAT !!! The main characters attack her lack of beauty and scars as if they are her main flaw. Well, I argue that they shouldn't be a flaw AT ALL. One of the main messages of the book was that everyone had inner beauty no matter what they looked like - whether they had "strange" wolf-like features or a ... mechanical arm. But that clearly flew out the window when writing this book. -_- <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> *end rant*<br><br>sad right now at the unfulfilled potential of a conclusion that could have done this incredible series justice. -W out.<br><br><u>BEFORE READING</u><br>ARE YOU SERIOUS?!!! 2015?! 1 whole year. BRB CRYING.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391973401ra/8482611.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1 whole year without this conclusion that I DESPERATELY need. 1 more year. *gasp* NEED MORE CINDER AND KAI. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386374474ra/7350257.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385601950ra/7183228.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380812584ra/3124630.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>NEED MORE OF THIS SERIES. *gasping*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/665691.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="362904522660073707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

This narrator nailed it! 💕<br/><br/>MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/11/winter-by-marissa-meyer.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447185939ra/16967102.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>I CAN'T BELIEVE IT'S OVER!</b> <b>I was so happy with the way this book went and the way it ended.   <span id="freeText2258986015521192034" style="display:none">RE-READ AUDIO 2017. This narrator nailed it! 💕<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/11/winter-by-marissa-meyer.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447185939ra/16967102.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I CAN'T BELIEVE IT'S OVER!</b> <b>I was so happy with the way this book went and the way it ended. Enjoy!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447302814i/16984557.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the dynamics between all of the characters. Each character in this book brings something to the table and have their own story and form of bad areseness! <br><br>Not one minute did this book get boring. Everything in the book was layered in a perfect way, but this is just my opinion. I had one part I wished could have been more revenge filling for me, but as most of those that read my reviews, know I'm into the hulk smash, wipe the floor with them kind of revenge.. but I'm still happy :) <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447302814ra/16984558.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>•••••••••••••• EXCERPTS •••••••••••••<br><br><b>"Did I tell you I saw snow when I was on Earth?"</b><br><b>Winter stopped walking, her eyes going wide. "Why does the queen want to kill you?" "She believes I'm a threat to her crown</b><br> <b>Scarlet snorted, an exhausted sound that didn't carry half as much derision as it should have. "Really? If there is anyone in this room who is guilty of royal treason, it is the woman sitting on that throne." She fixed her eyes on Levana. Cinder kicked him. He huffed. "Fine. You first.</b><br><br>••••••••••••••••<br><br><b>Scarlet leaned against the regolith wall. "My father was a liar and a drunk. My mother left when I was a kid and never looked back. I witnessed a man kill my grandmother and then rip out her throat with his teeth. I was kept in a cage for six weeks. I was forced to cut off my own finger. I'm pretty sure I'm falling in love with a guy who has been genetically modified and mentally programmed to be a predator. So all things considered, I'd say I have a fair amount of scattered pieces myself."</b><br><br>••••••••••••••••••<br><br><b>"Fight with me," she said, when enough time had passed and neither she nor Scarlet had been devoured. "I will not control you. I will not torture you. Help me end Levana's rule and we will all have our freedom."</b><br> <b>Alpha Strom met the eyes of a handful of soldiers-the other alphas, she presumed-before fixing a penetrating look on her. "I cannot speak for the entire regiment," he finally said, "but I will accept your offer. If you swear to never control us as they have done, my pack will fight for your revolution."<b><br> <b>Some of the men nodded. Others growled, but Winter thought it was a growl of agreement. In response, she lifted her nose to the cavern ceiling and howled.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447302814i/16984561.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>•••••••• END EXCERPTS •••••••••••<br><br>This book was a joy and I will miss reading further adventures, but the wonderful thing about books... we can always come back to them. <br><br><br><b>FOR RYU......</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447302814ra/16984562.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b></b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_838071872" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838071872" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/838071872?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=jerk-of-my-dreams">jerk-of-my-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=weres-shapeshifters">weres-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=here-be-slaves">here-be-slaves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=unread-ya-science-fiction">unread-ya-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer838071872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6327746805351040366"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/11/review-winter-by-marissa-meyer-jessicadhaluska.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>I've been a champion of THE LUNAR CHRONICLES for years now. I saw CINDER featured for months and months on <b>
  <a href='http://www.fantasticfiction.co.uk/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantastic Fiction</a>
</b> (b/c before I started using Goodreads), and I was simultaneously intrigued and horrified by the concept of a sci-fi YA retelling of a fairy tale. Honestly, I don't remember what finally convinced me to pick it up. I was just glad I did.<br/><br/>Now I'm not so sure. The first two books were fantastic, and while I wasn’t quite as fond of the third, it wasn</span>
  <span id="freeText6327746805351040366" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/11/review-winter-by-marissa-meyer-jessicadhaluska.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>I've been a champion of THE LUNAR CHRONICLES for years now. I saw CINDER featured for months and months on <b>
  <a href="http://www.fantasticfiction.co.uk/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantastic Fiction</a>
</b> (b/c before I started using Goodreads), and I was simultaneously intrigued and horrified by the concept of a sci-fi YA retelling of a fairy tale. Honestly, I don't remember what finally convinced me to pick it up. I was just glad I did.<br><br>Now I'm not so sure. The first two books were fantastic, and while I wasn’t quite as fond of the third, it wasn’t awful.<br><br>BUT.<br><br>After finishing WINTER, I added two new bookshelves (a record) to my Goodreads collection:<br><br>1. you-should-be-ashamed-of-yourself<br>2. are-you-effing-kidding-me<br><br>Why?<br><br>For a multitude of reasons. <br><br>And for the second time this year (though for very different reasons), this will be a two-part review--a nonspoilery review first, followed by a spoiler-tagged RANT.<br><br><b>I hate WINTER, Part I:</b><br><br><b>1. Unexplained plot threads.</b><br><br>Threads. As in plural. I can only talk about one here, but there are many more, and two of them are HUGE. <br><br>Meyer got away without having to focus on the romantic evolution of most of her MC couples in WINTER. Cinder and Kai have been around since book 1. Scarlet and Wolf, almost as long, plus Wolf’s animal instincts make it believable. Winter and Jacin, b/c they’ve loved each other FOREVER. <br><br>Cress and Thorne? Not so much. <br><br>Cress has very real, very legitimate issues with Thorne and his incorrigible need to flirt with any and all present females, and Thorne is a life-long womanizer. But these obstacles never get directly addressed. We're just supposed to accept that Cress is "different" and Thorne <i>really has changed</i>, without any concrete evidence to support those claims. <br><br>Call me cynical, but I'd learned that lesson by the time I was twenty.<br><br><b>2. Winter and Jacin feel like guests in their own story.</b><br><br>I didn't go back and do the math, but I'd guess that only 5 - 10% of this monster was spent on Winter and Jacin as a couple. I'll grant you that the time spent on their coupleness was fantastic. I'll even say that it was as fantastic as the stuff we saw with Scarlet and Wolf (my personal favorite couple). <br><br>BUT. <br><br>These moments were so few and far between that they were completely overwhelmed by ALL THE OTHER THINGS. <br><br>In the end, I was convinced their love was real. I just didn't care.<br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412267ra/810672.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br><b>3. ALL THE OTHER THINGS.</b><br><br>There was entirely too much happening in this book. I don't know if Meyer couldn't maintain the quality of writing we've become accustomed to, or if she was frazzled from trying to fit everything in, but WINTER was choked with clumsily handled side plots.<br><br>Parts of the story evolution are so lazy, it's almost like Meyer expected the leftover adrenaline from all the BAD THINGS, the one area where she continued to excel (unexpectedly dropping truly horrible obstacles on our MCs), to carry us right over the discrepancies. <br><br>And for a lot of people that probably worked. <br><br>BUT. <br><br>Not me.<br><br><b>4. EXTREME repetition for added shock factor.</b><br><br>I almost DNF-ed this book. I was 80% into it, but I did not care, I was ready to take all 800+ pages to the shooting range and use it for target practice. <br><br>Why?<br><br>B/c I was so over Lunars taking control of 1/2 of our MC couples and making them try to kill the other half. <br><br>YES. I get it. Lunars SUCK. They will steal your free will and make you do really bad stuff. LIKE KILL YOUR FRIENDS or your ONE TRUE LOVE. <br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445808667i/16704626.jpg" width="236" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>ALSO, death was constantly imminent. Someone(s) would get captured, execution would be inevitable, HA HA, just kidding! Escape, wheeeeeeee! <br><br>Over and over and OVER again.<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427991078i/14347821.jpg" width="400" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br><b>5. How the end played out (and this is my NUMERO UNO problem, FYI):</b><br><br>This isn't really a spoiler, but if you're one of those readers who wants to go into a book completely blind, I'd skip this part. Actually, if you're one of those types of readers, I'd avoid reviews entirely. <br><br>Anyway, Levana is pure evil. We know this. We've known this for a looooooong time. She has done so many horrible, shocking, despicable things, and she is CRAZY. <br><br>She has to die. The end. <br><br>The question is how to do it? How do we take down this master of bioelectricity manipulation? <br><br>The possibilities are endless.<br><br>So imagine my surprise and OUTRAGE when a huge part of that plan involves revealing to the world what Levana looks like underneath that veil.<br><br>I call:<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447525657i/17015938.jpg" width="236" height="236" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>And I'm furious all over again. <br><br>I'm furious b/c I HATE Levana, and I'm furious that I have to be outraged on her behalf. I'm furious b/c what in the effing hell is the point of having a cyborg mechanic for a princess, if you're going to have her go all Mean Girl on the crazy chick?<br><br><b>B/c Levana is a rabid dog. <br><br>You don't kick a rabid dog. You don't jeer and laugh at it b/c UGLY. You put it out of it's misery. The-effing-end.</b><br><br>And that's it for the first portion of of my review. I can't adequately communicate how disappointing WINTER by Marissa Meyer is without spoilers, but I hope you at least get the gist. This is the worst last book in a previously beloved series I have ever encountered. I did not know it was possible to be this underwhelmed, this unhappily surprised, this ANGRY about a book from an author whose past work had been stellar. I’m undecided about whether or not the early installments warrant an overall recommendation. Your call. Ugh.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I hate WINTER, Part II:</b><br><br>NOT kidding, there are spoilers EVERYWHERE in there. DO NOT click unless you've already read the book, or have no intentions of ever doing so. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br><b>1. Unexplained and DANGLING plot threads (in order of least to greatest importance, according to ME):</b><br><br><b>The unidentified RAT.</b> Yes, Cress was primarily responsible for all the spyware in Kai's palace, but no matter how great a hacker you are, you can't manifest cameras and listening devices in strategic locations. <br><br>So how did they get there?<br><br>I was convinced Torin had been brainwashed, but even without him being the culprit, someone else had to be. But who?<br><br>I guess we'll never know.<br><br><b>Iko's personality chip.</b> This is how it went down: <br><br>a. Garan's unnecessary software updates are mentioned, making it more than obvious that something is hinky. <br><br>b. Uprising. <br><br>c. Cinder unconscious for three days. <br><br>d. Cinder wakes up and IMMEDIATELY calls for meeting of world powers, where she announces Garan's research is, and has always been, in Iko's wacky personality chip.<br><br>Okay, fine. I'd pretty much guessed as much based the aforementioned OBVIOUS clue. BUT. Cinder never actually confirmed this speculation. And based on Iko's surprise at the announcement, it's clear Cinder didn't check it out off-page either.<br><br>That's a NEAT trick.<br><br><b>Wolf's (further) genetic modifications.</b> Wolf spent his early years as one of Levana's super soldiers in constant fear that he'd fail somehow and end up back on the operating table. Everything he did from the time he woke up from his initial mods was in pursuit of avoiding the lot of the majority of his soldier brethren. <br><br>B/c more animal than human. B/c slaves to instincts. B/c specifically created to be violent, remorseless killing machines. <br><br>And when he woke up, I'll admit I was concerned. In fact, of ALL the Bad Things, this one upset me most. B/c LOVE Wolf. And his fear of this exact fate was palpable. <br><br>But oh, look at that . . . He's pretty much the same Wolf he's always been except for a few cosmetic changes. Presumably b/c Scarlet (mate/alpha/blah/whatever), but who can really say, b/c Meyer certainly didn't. <br><br>ALL that buildup, all that fear, all that pressure . . . all for nothing, apparently.<br><br><b>2. ALL THE OTHER THINGS:</b><br><br><b>I've already said waaaaay too much was happening in this book</b> . . . Meyer got lazy. Some of that laziness is evident in the unresolved plot lines, but it's also a problem with various foreshadowings. <br><br>In laying the groundwork for future plot twists, instead of the subtlety, the carefully inserted details that thrilled us in hindsight, we got this:<br><br><blockquote>
<i>“Why did I pass out?” Cinder interrupted. <br>Crouching beside the couch, Jacin felt for the pulse in Cinder’s wrist. After a short silence, he let it drop down again. “Stress, probably, along with your physical reaction to having the portscreen connected to your”—he gestured to her general head area—“ computer thing.” <br>“And you call </i>me <i>squeamish,” said Thorne. <br><b>Cinder squinted. “I passed out from stress?</b> That’s it?” <br>“I believe the princess term is </i>fainted<i>,” said Thorne.</i>
</blockquote>
<br>Riiiiiight. After being completely submerged in water, after a 4+ story swan dive, she passed out b/c STRESS. <br><br>Do I even need to address all the problems with this? <br><br>How 'bout I limit it to this one: in the past, every, single time Cinder has passed out/come close to passing out, her computer brain exploded into a frenzy of cautions and warnings. <br><br>BUT.<br><br>Not this time. <br><br>So somehow, I just wasn't surprised when it was later revealed that Cinder did in fact have something seriously wrong with her. <br><br><b>Shades of Panem.</b><br><br>That's pretty self-explanatory, but Luna, its outer districts and their function, the inability to communicate between the districts and thus rebel in force . . . It all felt strangely familiar . . . <br><br><b>There were also RIDICULOUSLY overused plot devices.</b> Like this:<br><br><blockquote><i>“I accept,” Cinder said, dazed. She kept hold of Levana’s trigger finger but allowed Levana to lower the gun. Cinder held out her hand and Levana stared at it for a moment before reaching forward and setting the gun into Cinder’s palm. <br><b>In the same movement, she grabbed the forgotten knife and lurched forward, driving the blade into Cinder’s heart.</b></i></blockquote>
<br>Are. You. Effing kidding me? <br><br><b>3. EXTREME overuse of Lunar gifts for added shock factor:</b> <br><br>This primarily manifests in the utilization of mind control, which I already mentioned. <br><br>What I couldn't say is that in quick succession, a random thaumaturge forces Scarlet to try to kill Wolf, AIMERY (the swine) forces Winter to try to strangle Jacin, and Levana forces Thorne to attack DAMN EVERYBODY, but especially Cress, whom he stabs IN THE GUT.<br><br>And that's not the only time something like this happens, it's just the most memorable. <br><br>SIDE NOTE: I've decided to add "No mind control" to my list of rules b/c it makes everything too damn easy. <br><br><b>4. Inconsistency:</b><br><br><b>Winter.</b> She is as CRAY as Levana, but in a far less nefarious way. <br><br>Her crazy is self-inflicted, b/c she refuses--I mean <i>absolutely</i> refuses--to use her Lunar gift. <br><br>Until she doesn't. Refuse, that is. <br><br>Don't misunderstand, I didn't want her to kill Jacin. And if this was the only instance of inconsistency, I probably would've let it slide. <br><br>But it wasn't.<br><br><b>Jacin's parents weren't executed, as ordered.</b> Again, it's not like I wanted his parents to die. <br><br>But it's constantly reiterated that Levana does <i>exactly</i> what she says she's going to do. That's why Scarlet cut off her own finger. That's why Winter contemplated the uselessness of Dude-on-trial-for-rescuing/attempting-to-rescue-his-shell-child's begging for mercy for his family, b/c once Levana says they're to be killed/enslaved, that is what <i>will</i> happen. <br><br>And yet, Jacin's parents escaped their fate b/c they'd conveniently relocated? <br><br>LIKE THAT WOULD STOP HER. Especially when she went there herself to dose Winter with THE PLAGUE. <br><br><b>Levana's complete and total meltdown b/c true appearance revealed.</b> Let me see if I've got this right . . . <br><br>Levana, so thoroughly insane and DETERMINED that she both convinces herself that she is the best woman for the job of Queen, then carries out various horrific plots to attain her selfless goal, just gives up when the world sees her real face? Is so distraught that she can barely control the most basic bioelectrical manipulations?<br><br>Hmm . . . that's mighty convenient for Cinder . . . but somehow I'm not convinced.<br><br><b>5. How the end played out:</b><br><br><blockquote><i>Seeing Levana on the palace steps was the first time Iko had ever seen the Lunar queen, and her scarred face made Iko wish she wasn’t immune to glamours. After years of hearing about the queen’s famous beauty, the truth had been something of a letdown. <br><b>But the truth was out. Thanks to Cinder’s video, now everyone knew what lurked beneath the illusion.</b></i></blockquote>
<br>You know what I took away from this book? <br><br>Winter is pretty. She's so, so pretty. She might be the prettiest girl in the world. And, BONUS, she's <i>naturally</i> pretty. <br><br>Levana is ugly. So very ugly. Sickeningly ugly. B/c scarred in childhood trauma involving FIRE. <br><br><b>You:</b> How awful! <br><b>Me:</b> YES. It is.<br><br>See, I went to school with a girl who had pulled a pot of boiling water on her head when she was a toddler, so I know <i>exactly</i> what that type of injury looks like. The rough, uneven scar tissue. The way that scar tissue pulls down the corner of your eye and mouth . . . <br><br>It is permanent, it is (superficially) hideous, and even if she hadn't been one of the nicest people I'd ever met, I would NEVER have been able to bring myself to use such a tragic accident against her. <br><br>Some things are beyond the pale.<br><br>But Meyer made the results of a similar accident the main weakness of our sociopathic, megalomaniac villain. Our villain--whom I DESPISED, for a MULTITUDE of excellent reasons--but whose #1 goal in the midst of her madness was to be LOVED. <br><br>So let's run her out of town b/c UGLY. <br><br>That's definitely where our focus should be. Not on the scheming and machinations, not on the infanticide, the sororicide, not on commandeering her people's children for her army and her experiments, but on her scars. On her physical flaws. <br><br>You disgust me.<br><br>And I don't want to hear any, "How else could they have defeated her?" arguments. That's not my job. That was Meyer's job. And I think she failed. Miserably. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472888024" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Glitches (Lunar Chronicles 0.5)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351598724" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1)</a>
</b><br><b>

</b><br><b>

<div id="review_1476608071" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1476608071" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1476608071?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=favorites-2016">favorites-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1476608071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10048353816910577702">Meh. <br/><br/>That’s really all I have to say.<br/><br/>This book is very, very long (it has tissue-paper pages! That’s how you know a YA book is too damn long). It introduces more characters I don’t care about, allowing me to realize that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1348947342' rel='nofollow noopener'>I really only care about Cress and Thorne</a>. It spends a hundred thousand million years wrapping up every loose end, and still the plotline and conclusion manage to feel unsatisfying.<br/><br/>I really don’t have much to say beyond that.<br/><br/>The fact that this book is 827 pages long and I can’t </span>
  <span id="freeText10048353816910577702" style="display:none">Meh. <br /><br />That’s really all I have to say.<br /><br />This book is very, very long (it has tissue-paper pages! That’s how you know a YA book is too damn long). It introduces more characters I don’t care about, allowing me to realize that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1348947342" rel="nofollow noopener">I really only care about Cress and Thorne</a>. It spends a hundred thousand million years wrapping up every loose end, and still the plotline and conclusion manage to feel unsatisfying.<br /><br />I really don’t have much to say beyond that.<br /><br />The fact that this book is 827 pages long and I can’t even summon up two paragraphs about it says it all.<br /><br />So let’s call that my bottom line and call it a day.<br /><br />-----------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />things about this book that are cute:<br />- Cress<br />- Thorne<br />- Cress and Thorne<br /><br />things about this book that are not cute:<br />- the fact that it is 827 PAGES LONG.<br /><br />review to comeee<br /><br />-----------<br /><br />uh, this book is...<i>long</i><br /><br />-----------<br /><br />if this book doesn't break my heart and make me cry i Will demand a refund</span>
  <a data-text-id="10048353816910577702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_674889220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674889220" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/674889220?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bubbling-under-5-stars">bubbling-under-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=fearless-protagonists">fearless-protagonists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june">pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=laugh-out-loud-humor">laugh-out-loud-humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer674889220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11372101046491864390"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I can't believe this is happening. I can't fight like this, or start a revolution, or be a queen. I can't do anything like this. I'm literally broken."<br/><br/>Iko settled a hand on Cinder's shoulder. "Yeah, but broken isn't the same as unfixable."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172466ra/17389411.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Winter isn't perfect. Marissa Meyer has some <i>very</i> big shoes to fill. Expectations are high, fans are passionate... but I do feel she left us with a largely satisfying ending.<br/><br/>I know what a lot of non-readers are wondering: does it drag? Surprisingl</span>
  <span id="freeText11372101046491864390" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I can't believe this is happening. I can't fight like this, or start a revolution, or be a queen. I can't do anything like this. I'm literally broken."<br><br>Iko settled a hand on Cinder's shoulder. "Yeah, but broken isn't the same as unfixable."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172466ra/17389411.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Winter isn't perfect. Marissa Meyer has some <i>very</i> big shoes to fill. Expectations are high, fans are passionate... but I do feel she left us with a largely satisfying ending.<br><br>I know what a lot of non-readers are wondering: does it drag? Surprisingly, no. At 800+ pages, it starts fast and pulls no punches. Admittedly, it slows near the middle, but nowhere near enough to make me want to skip or put down the book.<br><br>Some reviewers were upset with the repetition. Characters get captured, rescued, separated, then rinse and repeat. I disagree it isn't necessary. A revolution isn't easy and Meyer portrays the confusion and frustration nicely. <br><br>What I think <i>is</i> unnecessary is what happens to Wolf after he's captured in the latter half. Why? Why does it happen? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It doesn't affect his relationship with Scarlet or his personality. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>My guess—and I'm pretty sure I'm right—is Meyer needed make some waves for the Scarlet/Wolf ship. Everyone else had their problems: Kai is supposed to marry Levana; Thorne and Cress are caught in that adorable, frustrating period of does-he-or-she-like-me?; and Winter is a freaking princess while Jacin is a lowly guard. A lot of pressure for nothing.<br><br>So, new characters: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>[Jacin:] "She wants to kill you, Princess."<br><br>Winter shivered, first with the intensity of his words, and second with their meaning. She supposed such a declaration would have shocked her, but ever since Levana had given her these scars, she had been expecting this."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Winter is named after the character, but it isn't so much her story as it is Cinder's. But it's a minor annoyance. We knew from day one it was <i>Cinder's</i> story and about <i>Cinder</i> taking her rightful throne as Queen Serenity/Sailor Moon. Oops, I mean, Queen of Luna.<br><br>See, I'm not always a nitpicking bitch queen.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172466ra/17389412.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What we do see of Winter is fascinating. She's a complex character, far more morally ambiguous than Cinder is. You don't see it at first because she's sweet and kind and a little mad from Lunar sickness (Winter refuses to use her power and it slowly drives her crazy), but she knows she's gorgeous and uses it to manipulate people sometimes. <br><br>What can I say? I'm a sucker for a femme fatale.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172466ra/17389413.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Her portrayal of mental illness is intriguing.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"You want me to be fixed, don't you?"<br><br>Jacin drew back, as if she'd thrown something at him. "You're not broken."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>It reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7105371.Leah_Raeder" title="Leah Raeder" rel="nofollow noopener">Leah Raeder</a>'s style. Winter's madness is a part of her, no matter how others deny it. <br><br>You are not your mental illness. I stay by that one hundred percent. But it's some of you. One percent or seventy, it affects your daily life and personality. As long as you don't let it win.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172466ra/17389414.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172466ra/17389415.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172466ra/17389416.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Got off-topic a bit there. I'm amazed Marissa can juggle so many POVs, each with their own distinctive voice. I didn't count, but I'm pretty sure there's at least ten. <i>Ten</i>. Most writers can barely handle two. I never confuse Cress for Cinder, or Kai for Wolf. That's how good she is.<br><br>Cress and Thorne's relationship could have been developed better. I understand why Cress likes him, but not so much Thorne. A little more leading-up scenes and it'd be perfect.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172466ra/17389417.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Am I the only one who was sad Levana died? I know she's a power-hungry bitch, but <i>damn</i>. Girl had a hard life. I grew attached to her in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22489107.Fairest__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_5_" title="Fairest (The Lunar Chronicles, #3.5) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>A stunning conclusion to an amazing series. So when does <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18584855.Heartless" title="Heartless by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Heartless</a> come out?<br><br><br><b>Cover reveal:</b> Slightly underwhelmed with the cover. I expected it to be darker, like an apple dripping blood or something. <br><br>8 more months!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386539623i/7386904._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Pre-review</b>: Holy crap, 800 pages? What is this, a Stephen King novel?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11372101046491864390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
