        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1320574400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1109725096431542388"><u>My Reviews for this series:</u><br/>•<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277490539?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fairest</a><br/>•<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304153759?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stars Above</a><br/>•<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1271493655?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinder</a><br/>•<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290195047?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scarlet</a><br/>•<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1291148115?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cress</a><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447948960ra/17072061.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This finale to the <i>Lunar Chronicles</i> finds Cinder on a mission to take her rightful place on the throne of Luna, as she is the lost princess Selene.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447949899ra/17072292.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Winter</i> faces a major pacing problem. It's over 800 pages and a lot of it is just blah blah. It reminds me of a video game with too many tedious side quests and overlong cutscenes that you can't skip through. While there's plenty of action, the meat to garnish ratio here is not filling</span>
  <span id="freeText1109725096431542388" style="display:none"><u>My Reviews for this series:</u><br>•<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277490539?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a><br>•<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304153759?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Stars Above</a><br>•<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1271493655?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a><br>•<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290195047?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a><br>•<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1291148115?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Cress</a><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447948960ra/17072061.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This finale to the <i>Lunar Chronicles</i> finds Cinder on a mission to take her rightful place on the throne of Luna, as she is the lost princess Selene.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447949899ra/17072292.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Winter</i> faces a major pacing problem. It's over 800 pages and a lot of it is just blah blah. It reminds me of a video game with too many tedious side quests and overlong cutscenes that you can't skip through. While there's plenty of action, the meat to garnish ratio here is not filling. A good 300 pages could have been cut without the audience missing anything important.<br><br>Further, I hate to say this but for a story that is so progressive about minorities and women in STEM, some of the characters are just flat. Nearly all of the men are interchangeable and it takes a second to remember them and they are mostly only important in relation to the women they are paired with. I get it if Meyer is trying to make some sort of reverse-Bechdel commentary here, but I doubt these books are supposed to have that kind of depth.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447340528ra/16989784.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>You can tell the technology is advanced because each time someone uses a portscreen, they don't have to let out that sigh of frustration because they have to x out of an ad asking them to download an app when they go to a mobile site. Of course, even with adblocking apps like Crystal, this is too much of a fantasy to even hope for in our modern times.<br><br>Even with all of its problems, I have to say that this cover is my favorite of the entire series:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1447171461l/13206900.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(But the whole apple thing is kinda forced here in how it's implemented, tbh.)</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1274162026" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1274162026" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1274162026?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141340241" href="/book/show/25774272-winter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1274162026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14324620591299843880"><i>"Broken isn't the same as unfixable.”</i><br/><br/>A grand finale!<br/><br/>This had everything I'm looking for in a conclusion of a series. Everyone got a satisfying and even happily ever after. Satisfying is actually the best word to describe this novel. Often the last installment of a good series is a let-down (<i> End of Days </i> or <i>Clockwork Princess</i>).<br/>But this one had it all: suspense, romance and diversity (even though I really missed glbt-characters).<br/>Great world-building and character-depth. Feminism.<br/><br/>I am very thankfu</span>
  <span id="freeText14324620591299843880" style="display:none"><i>"Broken isn't the same as unfixable.”</i><br /><br />A grand finale!<br /><br />This had everything I'm looking for in a conclusion of a series. Everyone got a satisfying and even happily ever after. Satisfying is actually the best word to describe this novel. Often the last installment of a good series is a let-down (<i> End of Days </i> or <i>Clockwork Princess</i>).<br />But this one had it all: suspense, romance and diversity (even though I really missed glbt-characters).<br />Great world-building and character-depth. Feminism.<br /><br />I am very thankful for Marissa Meyer writing <i> the Lunar Chronicles </i>. Every single book was an amazing read and I can't wait for her new projects.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781410485908" href="/book/show/31196119-winter">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2553182915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16484615741700223551">never in my life would i have thought that i needed a sci-fi retelling of all the classic fairy tales. and yet here i am, four books and one amazing series later, shocked at how i could have even lasted this long without it. <br/><br/>its quite difficult for me to rate and review this as just one book in a series, because this was honestly one of the best conclusions i have ever read. it was such a wonderful culmination of all the previous books, put into one. it truly felt like a finale, showcasing and c</span>
  <span id="freeText16484615741700223551" style="display:none">never in my life would i have thought that i needed a sci-fi retelling of all the classic fairy tales. and yet here i am, four books and one amazing series later, shocked at how i could have even lasted this long without it. <br /><br />its quite difficult for me to rate and review this as just one book in a series, because this was honestly one of the best conclusions i have ever read. it was such a wonderful culmination of all the previous books, put into one. it truly felt like a finale, showcasing and celebrating what makes these books so great.<br /><br />there are a lot of positives about this, but i think the characters are the biggest accomplishment of this series. lets face it, the characters are the real reason why any of us continued with these books and i know we all have our favourites (<i>cough</i> WOLF <i>cough</i>). but whats especially impressive is how meyer took previously well-known characters and completely transformed them into a marvellous individuals of her own making. it was so entertaining to get to know them all in such a new light. and its these characters that i will forever remember when it comes to these books. <br /><br />there isnt much else i can say that hasnt already been said about this book and series. so if you havent picked up this series or need to complete it, do it as soon as possible. you wont regret it - i promise!!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16484615741700223551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661654089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5997910962376301861"><i>That's</i> how you end a series. I am in love! <br/><br/>A star for each one of my ships:<br/>*Scarlet & Wolf, forever my favorites. They, I think, have had the roughest journey of all, but they're love also seems the strongest. They never waver, especially in this book. <br/>*Cress & Thorne, who fully stole my heart in <i>Winter</i>. They are adorable beyond words, and so very, very perfect for each other.<br/>*Winter & Jacin, with their childhood love turned into something far fiercer and truer. They are each other's rocks in a </span>
  <span id="freeText5997910962376301861" style="display:none"><i>That's</i> how you end a series. I am in love! <br /><br />A star for each one of my ships:<br />*Scarlet &amp; Wolf, forever my favorites. They, I think, have had the roughest journey of all, but they're love also seems the strongest. They never waver, especially in this book. <br />*Cress &amp; Thorne, who fully stole my heart in <i>Winter</i>. They are adorable beyond words, and so very, very perfect for each other.<br />*Winter &amp; Jacin, with their childhood love turned into something far fiercer and truer. They are each other's rocks in a world full of crazy.<br />*Kai &amp; Cinder, still a little awkward, but endearing as they're finally able to be a unit.<br /><br />I love them all. In that order, because sometimes I like to play favorites.<br /><br />And a star for every other brilliant thing Marissa does with her final book. Tense sequences, pacing that, even with over 800 pages, <i>never</i> lets up, the descriptive lunar setting, the number of times she ripped my heart out and left me breathless, dialogue that will have you laughing one minute, swooning the next, and fist pumping a second later, characters who are just so... <i>them</i>. One of my favorite things about this series is how unique each personality is, each romance is, each friendship is. All the different dynamics make me so damn giddy. I will love this motley crew of the Rampion - including Iko, still boy crazy, still hilarious - until the stars fade. Already I miss them dearly. <br /><br />Bravo, Ms. Meyer. Bravo.<br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="http://www.loveatfirstpage.org/2015/11/20/mini-reviews-21-all-about-ya/" rel="nofollow noopener">Love at First Page</a>.</span>

<div id="review_1102204518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1102204518" />
    <a title="Dorreh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh"><img alt="Dorreh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565727363p2/22599584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1102204518?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorreh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorreh" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh">Dorreh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1102204518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15630727341307862280">No one touch me, I'm very fragile right now!!!<br/><br/>Oh my Gaaawwwwddddddd<br/><br/>What was that?! What splendid tragically heartbreaking exhilarating heart warming masterpiece of a conclusion was that? <br/><br/>Okay, deeeeeeppp breaths.........<br/><br/>Now to begin my review; first of all 823 pages of a story it was indeed. This was easily two books fit into one. Secondly they all finally got their happily ever afters, so I'm a messy ball of goo right now. <br/><br/>The book started of with a slightly slower pace, then elevated slowly as</span>
  <span id="freeText15630727341307862280" style="display:none">No one touch me, I'm very fragile right now!!!<br /><br />Oh my Gaaawwwwddddddd<br /><br />What was that?! What splendid tragically heartbreaking exhilarating heart warming masterpiece of a conclusion was that? <br /><br />Okay, deeeeeeppp breaths.........<br /><br />Now to begin my review; first of all 823 pages of a story it was indeed. This was easily two books fit into one. Secondly they all finally got their happily ever afters, so I'm a messy ball of goo right now. <br /><br />The book started of with a slightly slower pace, then elevated slowly as the book progressed. I admit with the slow pace of CRESS, seeing the number of pages in this one scared me a bit, but that anxious feeling began to evaporate as soon as it condensed. <br />The plot was well made and easily interpreted, it answered most, if not all, of the questions I had. It gave way to the separate unwinding of all the build up that had been made in its predecessor novel. <br /><br />I loved cinder from the the very beginning, and her badass mechanic toughness got me going so early on, I was sure I would continue this series. But then when I read SCARLET, I was like holy mother, there is a second to main character that I ship more than the main. I'm not sure if that's even possible in the world of books, because we all ship the main protagonist then love her beta's (pun intended), but in this case I knew I was hooked on scarlet and wolf and that did NOT change. <br /><br />I guess the best part of this whole series for me was the fact that it was four separate stories that met halfway in a beautifully and delicately carved masterpiece to make one whole story. So many characters each with their own story to tell. And somehow it all worked together perfectly, no hiccups or shortcomings. I admit I wanted more of a happy in happily ever after for winter, but I assume there is more to her in the stars above novellas. <br /><br />Overall this concluding novel, was intriguing, action filled, exhilaratingly heart warming, and about another hundred something adjectives I could use, but I think I've made my point......<br /><br />I would recommend this series to anyone that loves a good story and plot with a brilliant idea based characterization and incredibly authentic setting. I hope anyone who read this series enjoyed it as much as I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15630727341307862280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1232089616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" href="/user/show/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud">Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1232089616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2586737437192086169"><b>Solid 4.5 STARS. </b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Do me a favor, Princess. <br/>The next time someone says they're going to kill you, <br/>don't just let them.” </i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493353459ra/22606298.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I finished this! Again. <br/>They left me. Again. <br/>It's a bittersweet feeling. On one hand, I am completely satisfied with how Meyer decided to tie things up, but then on the other, i wouldn't have minded another book. Things felt a little rushed at times? <br/><br/>The only complaint I have is Thorne and Cress's relationship. It feels wrong? I don't know about you guys but Cress is like a </span>
  <span id="freeText2586737437192086169" style="display:none"><b>Solid 4.5 STARS. </b><br><br><b>
  <i>“Do me a favor, Princess. <br>The next time someone says they're going to kill you, <br>don't just let them.” </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493353459ra/22606298.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I finished this! Again. <br>They left me. Again. <br>It's a bittersweet feeling. On one hand, I am completely satisfied with how Meyer decided to tie things up, but then on the other, i wouldn't have minded another book. Things felt a little rushed at times? <br><br>The only complaint I have is Thorne and Cress's relationship. It feels wrong? I don't know about you guys but Cress is like a child in my head. Then we have Thorne who is a little narcissistic. Don't get me wrong, i still love the shit out of him. All I'm trying to say is he and Cress don't make much sense, or maybe as a couple, they lack development. His abrupt attraction for Cress was a bit inconceivable. I just didn't buy his sudden feelings for her. Where did they even come from? I would have preferred them just being friends. I think Thorne would be more suitable for someone like Scarlet and Cress with Wolf. <br><br><b>May is my reread month!</b><br><br>How do you feel about each character?<br><br><b>Iko:</b><br> She needs to get together with <b>AIDAN</b> and take over this horrible world. <br><br><b>Cress: </b>(Rapunzel)<br>A lost bunny in the wilds. Someone protect this cinnamon roll. <br><br><b>Thorne:</b>(Flynn Rider)<br> Silly, selfish . . is what he wants you to think. There is so much more to his character than just being the funny one. &lt;3<br><br><b>Scarlet:</b> (The Red Ridding Hood)<br>Ballsy AF! The sass on that one!<br><br><b>Wolf:</b> (Well, the Wolf!)<br> Alluring with his alpha male thing going on. Like, he is literally an alpha, not cringy ones we see so often. AND he loves tomatoes. <br><br><b>Winter: </b> (The Snow White)<br>A three-legged the most adorable puppy<br><br><b>Cinder: </b>(Cinderella)<br>Undaunted. This girl just never gives up.<br><br><b>Kai:</b>(The Prince Charming)<br> We love you, but where are the others?<br><br><b>Jacin:</b> (The Huntsman)<br>HIM! His character development was my most favorite. Such an ass but i can't help but love him. His transformation from one side to another left me awestruck. This boy is all over the place.</span>

          </span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YXOHNbdLL1x+e8rYorvoI4eTzKO/F4I6DI5LYa8GIqxbVe7nDBXmNNlQfrlVTuL8Ucwra3GaDF1X8A3QYkXQNg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Kc4MumsqgHpuhdBVo4M868RgOUOWTcfktnf+PcyIIhAT6GVo0HRJEsmuZDRUdjY0Ej/ei1jASYPtCbiMAcvQig==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
